  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/355b347e51bc93811d77d1279a7760e5aae2bcc0" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.338ex; width:11.836ex; height:3.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle y={\tfrac {1}{x_{1}x_{2}}}\;x\ .}"/></span>
</p><p>Consequence: for any pair of points <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle P,Q}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>P</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>Q</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P,Q}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/94b3c5b21ee2d8a12253a952e4c4b1733ceb0735" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.618ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="P,Q"/></span> of a chord there exists a <i>skew reflection</i> with an axis (set of fixed points) passing through the center of the hyperbola, which exchanges the points <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle P,Q}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>P</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>Q</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P,Q}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/94b3c5b21ee2d8a12253a952e4c4b1733ceb0735" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.618ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="P,Q"/></span> and leaves the hyperbola (as a whole) fixed. A skew reflection is a generalization of an ordinary reflection across a line <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle m}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>m</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle m}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.04ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="m"/></span>, where all point-image pairs are on a line perpendicular to <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle m}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>m</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle m}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a07d98bb302f3856cbabc47b2b9016692e3f7bc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.04ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="m"/></span>.
</p><p>Because a skew reflection leaves the hyperbola fixed, the pair of asymptotes is fixed, too. Hence the midpoint <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle M}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>M</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle M}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f82cade9898ced02fdd08712e5f0c0151758a0dd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.442ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="M"/></span> of a chord <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle PQ}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>P</mi>
        <mi>Q</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle PQ}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/56648d25dcb487300d460480dec33d3c713fe4ca" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.584ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="P Q"/></span> divides the related line segment <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\overline {P}}\,{\overline {Q}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mover>
            <mi>P</mi>
            <mo accent="false">&#x00AF;<!-- ¯ --></mo>
          </mover>
        </mrow>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mover>
            <mi>Q</mi>
            <mo accent="false">&#x00AF;<!-- ¯ --></mo>
          </mover>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\overline {P}}\,{\overline {Q}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/930a4a10daa8847acd1c73f83c2d90615c1037e2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.365ex; height:3.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\overline {P}}\,{\overline {Q}}}"/></span> between the asymptotes  into halves, too. This means that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle |P{\overline {P}}|=|Q{\overline {Q}}|}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mi>P</mi>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mover>
            <mi>P</mi>
            <mo accent="false">&#x00AF;<!-- ¯ --></mo>
          </mover>
        </mrow>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mi>Q</mi>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mover>
            <mi>Q</mi>
            <mo accent="false">&#x00AF;<!-- ¯ --></mo>
          </mover>
        </mrow>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle |P{\overline {P}}|=|Q{\overline {Q}}|}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/77949ca12e922a3a208494db46aaa72d327ffbbf" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.248ex; height:3.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle |P{\overline {P}}|=|Q{\overline {Q}}|}"/></span>. This property can be used for the construction of further points <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle Q}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>Q</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle Q}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8752c7023b4b3286800fe3238271bbca681219ed" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.838ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="Q"/></span> of the hyperbola if a point <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle P}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>P</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b4dc73bf40314945ff376bd363916a738548d40a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.745ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="P"/></span> and the asymptotes are given.
</p><p>If the chord degenerates into a <i>tangent</i>, then the touching point divides the line segment between the asymptotes in two halves.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Steiner_generation_of_a_hyperbola">Steiner generation of a hyperbola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Steiner generation of a hyperbola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-steiner-e.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hyperbel-steiner-e.svg/250px-Hyperbel-steiner-e.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hyperbel-steiner-e.svg/375px-Hyperbel-steiner-e.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Hyperbel-steiner-e.svg/500px-Hyperbel-steiner-e.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="366" data-file-height="274" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-steiner-e.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbola: Steiner generation</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbola_construction_-_parallelogram_method.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Hyperbola_construction_-_parallelogram_method.gif/200px-Hyperbola_construction_-_parallelogram_method.gif" decoding="async" width="200" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Hyperbola_construction_-_parallelogram_method.gif/300px-Hyperbola_construction_-_parallelogram_method.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Hyperbola_construction_-_parallelogram_method.gif 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbola_construction_-_parallelogram_method.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbola <i>y</i> = 1/<i>x</i>: Steiner generation</div></div></div>
<p>The following method to construct single points of a hyperbola relies on the <a href="/wiki/Steiner_conic" title="Steiner conic">Steiner generation of a non degenerate conic section</a>:
</p>
<dl><dd>Given two <a href="/wiki/Pencil_(mathematics)" title="Pencil (mathematics)">pencils</a> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle B(U),B(V)}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

        <mi>B</mi>

        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>B</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
        <mi>V</mi>
        <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle B(U),B(V)}</annotation>
  </semantics>

  <semantics>

        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>V</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle U,V}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7681409ec5fffdb272f536757c1211fe0151a9b2" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:4.604ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="U,V"/></span> (all lines containing <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle U}">

<p>For the generation of points of the hyperbola <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\tfrac {x^{2}}{a^{2}}}-{\tfrac {y^{2}}{b^{2}}}=1}">

    </mrow>

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f18d979f7a463de6227020a06a2652f7f0c03f91" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.671ex; width:12.198ex; height:4.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\tfrac {x^{2}}{a^{2}}}-{\tfrac {y^{2}}{b^{2}}}=1}"/></span> one uses the pencils at the vertices <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle V_{1},V_{2}}">

Let <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle P=(x_{0},y_{0})}">
  <semantics>

          <mi>x</mi>

A better idea is extending the points already constructed by symmetry (see animation).
</p><p><i>Remark:</i>
</p>
<ol><li>The Steiner generation exists for ellipses and parabolas, too.</li>
<li>The Steiner generation is sometimes called a <i>parallelogram method</i> because one can use other points rather than the vertices, which starts with a parallelogram instead of a rectangle.</li></ol>
<h2><span id="Inscribed_angles_for_hyperbolas_y_.3D_a.2F.28x_.E2.88.92_b.29_.2B_c_and_the_3-point-form"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Inscribed_angles_for_hyperbolas_y_=_a/(x_−_b)_+_c_and_the_3-point-form">Inscribed angles for hyperbolas <i>y</i> = <i>a</i>/(<i>x</i> − <i>b</i>) + <i>c</i> and the 3-point-form</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Inscribed angles for hyperbolas y = a/(x − b) + c and the 3-point-form">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-pws-s.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hyperbel-pws-s.svg/250px-Hyperbel-pws-s.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hyperbel-pws-s.svg/375px-Hyperbel-pws-s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hyperbel-pws-s.svg/500px-Hyperbel-pws-s.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="323" data-file-height="325" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-pws-s.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbola: inscribed angle theorem</div></div></div>

<p>Analogous to the <a href="/wiki/Inscribed_angle" title="Inscribed angle">inscribed angle</a> theorem for circles one gets the
</p><p><b>Inscribed angle theorem for hyperbolas:</b>,:<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>

<dl><dd>For four points  <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle P_{i}=(x_{i},y_{i}),\ i=1,2,3,4,\ x_{i}\neq x_{k},y_{i}\neq y_{k},i\neq k}">

<h2><span id="Orthogonal_tangents_.E2.80.93_orthoptic"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthogonal_tangents_–_orthoptic">Orthogonal tangents – orthoptic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Orthogonal tangents – orthoptic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Orthoptic-hyperbola-s.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Orthoptic-hyperbola-s.svg/220px-Orthoptic-hyperbola-s.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Orthoptic-hyperbola-s.svg/330px-Orthoptic-hyperbola-s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Orthoptic-hyperbola-s.svg/440px-Orthoptic-hyperbola-s.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="378" data-file-height="297" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Orthoptic-hyperbola-s.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbola with its orthoptic (magenta)</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Orthoptic_(geometry)" title="Orthoptic (geometry)">Orthoptic (geometry)</a></div>
<p>For a hyperbola <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {x^{2}}{a^{2}}}-{\frac {y^{2}}{b^{2}}}=1,\,a&gt;b}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <msup>
              <mi>x</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>2</mn>
              </mrow>
            </msup>
            <msup>
              <mi>a</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>2</mn>
              </mrow>
            </msup>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <msup>
              <mi>y</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>2</mn>
              </mrow>
            </msup>
            <msup>
              <mi>b</mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>2</mn>
              </mrow>
            </msup>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mn>1</mn>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mi>a</mi>
        <mo>&gt;</mo>
        <mi>b</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {x^{2}}{a^{2}}}-{\frac {y^{2}}{b^{2}}}=1,\,a&gt;b}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/79dae9b470b8f2e6d6eeadb9414e3a8dae15b9c8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:20.119ex; height:6.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\frac {x^{2}}{a^{2}}}-{\frac {y^{2}}{b^{2}}}=1,\,a&gt;b}"/></span> the intersection points of <i>orthogonal</i> tangents lie on the circle <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x^{2}+y^{2}=a^{2}-b^{2}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msup>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>+</mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>y</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>a</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>b</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x^{2}+y^{2}=a^{2}-b^{2}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5ddee401fba3af56fb1cb515cdd4da0015cf2040" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:17.714ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="x^{2}+y^{2}=a^{2}-b^{2}"/></span>. <br />
This circle is called the <i>orthoptic</i> of the given hyperbola.
</p><p>The tangents may belong to points on different branches of the hyperbola.
</p><p>In case of <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle a\leq b}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>a</mi>
        <mo>&#x2264;<!-- ≤ --></mo>
        <mi>b</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a\leq b}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/41558abc50886fdf38817495b243958d7b3dd39b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:5.326ex; height:2.343ex;" alt="a\leq b"/></span> there are no pairs of orthogonal tangents.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pole-polar_relation_for_a_hyperbola">Pole-polar relation for a hyperbola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Pole-polar relation for a hyperbola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-pol-s.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hyperbel-pol-s.svg/250px-Hyperbel-pol-s.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hyperbel-pol-s.svg/375px-Hyperbel-pol-s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Hyperbel-pol-s.svg/500px-Hyperbel-pol-s.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="248" data-file-height="226" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-pol-s.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbola: pole-polar relation</div></div></div>
<p>Any hyperbola can be described in a suitable coordinate system by an equation <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\tfrac {x^{2}}{a^{2}}}-{\tfrac {y^{2}}{b^{2}}}=1}">

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/49d068df673bcb491813b55e60e239bce8f170e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.317ex; height:2.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x=c,\ c\neq 0}"/></span> onto the point <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \left({\frac {a^{2}}{c}},0\right)\ .}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow>
          <mo>(</mo>
          <mrow>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mfrac>
                <msup>
                  <mi>a</mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mn>2</mn>
                  </mrow>
                </msup>

              </mfrac>
            </mrow>

            <mn>0</mn>

        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \left({\frac {a^{2}}{c}},0\right)\ .}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7f96865dffc35fb22ae440269b8b8c88bd21a3c3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:10.352ex; height:6.343ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \left({\frac {a^{2}}{c}},0\right)\ .}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Such a relation between points and lines generated by a conic is called <b>pole-polar relation</b> or just <i>polarity</i>. The pole is the point, the polar the line. See <a href="/wiki/Pole_and_polar" title="Pole and polar">Pole and polar</a>.
</p><p>By calculation one checks the following properties of the pole-polar relation of the hyperbola:
</p>
<ul><li>For a point (pole) <i>on</i> the hyperbola the polar is the tangent at this point (see diagram: <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle P_{1},\ p_{1}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>P</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>1</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mtext>&#xA0;</mtext>
        <msub>
          <mi>p</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>1</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P_{1},\ p_{1}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/52541841fd849efd2bb0fdc18fbea0821a7595f5" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:6.385ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle P_{1},\ p_{1}}"/></span>).</li>
<li>For a pole <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle P}">
  <semantics>

<p>Pole-polar relations exist for ellipses and parabolas, too.
</p>
<h2><span id="Hyperbola_as_an_affine_image_of_the_unit_hyperbola_x.C2.B2_.E2.80.93_y.C2.B2_.3D_1"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hyperbola_as_an_affine_image_of_the_unit_hyperbola_x²_–_y²_=_1">Hyperbola as an affine image of the unit hyperbola <i>x</i>² – <i>y</i>² = 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Hyperbola as an affine image of the unit hyperbola x² – y² = 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-aff-s.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Hyperbel-aff-s.svg/300px-Hyperbel-aff-s.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Hyperbel-aff-s.svg/450px-Hyperbel-aff-s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Hyperbel-aff-s.svg/600px-Hyperbel-aff-s.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="414" data-file-height="263" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-aff-s.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbola as an affine image of the unit hyperbola</div></div></div>
<p>Another definition of a hyperbola uses <a href="/wiki/Affine_transformation" title="Affine transformation">affine transformations</a>:
</p>
<dl><dd>Any <i>hyperbola</i> is the affine image of the unit hyperbola with equation <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x^{2}-y^{2}=1}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msup>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>y</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mn>1</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x^{2}-y^{2}=1}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/66b6dc015284f725f6537eb50fe4b20348cf0a5a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:11.7ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="x^2-y^2=1"/></span>.</dd></dl>
<p>An affine transformation of the Euclidean plane has the form <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\vec {x}}\to {\vec {f}}_{0}+A{\vec {x}}}">

            <mn>0</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>+</mo>
        <mi>A</mi>

        </mrow>

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e431e5943dc2b4d638036815189e4f26ea4d2b1c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.576ex; height:3.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\vec {x}}\to {\vec {f}}_{0}+A{\vec {x}}}"/></span>, where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle A}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>A</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle A}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7daff47fa58cdfd29dc333def748ff5fa4c923e3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.743ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="A"/></span> is a regular <a href="/wiki/Matrix_(mathematics)" title="Matrix (mathematics)">matrix</a> (its <a href="/wiki/Determinant" title="Determinant">determinant</a> is not 0) and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\vec {f}}_{0}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\vec {f}}_{0}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d1ae526b00782f0150985cd3fa027d82369c0abd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:2.719ex; height:3.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\vec {f}}_{0}}"/></span> is an arbitrary vector. If <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\vec {f}}_{1},{\vec {f}}_{2}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<h2><span id="Hyperbola_as_an_affine_image_of_the_hyperbola_y_.3D_1.2Fx"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hyperbola_as_an_affine_image_of_the_hyperbola_y_=_1/x">Hyperbola as an affine image of the hyperbola <i>y</i> = 1/<i>x</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Hyperbola as an affine image of the hyperbola y = 1/x">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-aff2.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Hyperbel-aff2.svg/300px-Hyperbel-aff2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Hyperbel-aff2.svg/450px-Hyperbel-aff2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Hyperbel-aff2.svg/600px-Hyperbel-aff2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="367" data-file-height="257" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-aff2.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbola as affine image of <i>y</i> = 1/<i>x</i></div></div></div>
<p>Because the unit hyperbola <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle x^{2}-y^{2}=1}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msup>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <msup>
          <mi>y</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mn>1</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x^{2}-y^{2}=1}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/66b6dc015284f725f6537eb50fe4b20348cf0a5a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:11.7ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="x^2-y^2=1"/></span> is affinely equivalent to the hyperbola <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle y=1/x}">

</p><p>The following properties of a hyperbola are easily proven using the representation of a hyperbola introduced in this section.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tangent_construction">Tangent construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Tangent construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-tang-s.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Hyperbel-tang-s.svg/220px-Hyperbel-tang-s.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Hyperbel-tang-s.svg/330px-Hyperbel-tang-s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Hyperbel-tang-s.svg/440px-Hyperbel-tang-s.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="324" data-file-height="247" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-tang-s.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tangent construction: asymptotes and <i>P</i> given → tangent</div></div></div>

<p>This property provides a way to construct the tangent at a point on the hyperbola.
</p><p>This property of a hyperbola is an affine version of the 3-point-degeneration of <a href="/wiki/Pascal%27s_theorem" title="Pascal&#39;s theorem">Pascal's theorem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

</p>

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\text{Area}}={\Big |}\det \left(t{\vec {f}}_{1},{\tfrac {1}{t}}{\vec {f}}_{2}\right){\Big |}={\Big |}\det \left({\vec {f}}_{1},{\vec {f}}_{2}\right){\Big |}=\cdots ={\frac {a^{2}+b^{2}}{4}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f0f2f93367bc247f2208c0097bcbc00cbd412578" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:60.341ex; height:5.676ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\text{Area}}={\Big |}\det \left(t{\vec {f}}_{1},{\tfrac {1}{t}}{\vec {f}}_{2}\right){\Big |}={\Big |}\det \left({\vec {f}}_{1},{\vec {f}}_{2}\right){\Big |}=\cdots ={\frac {a^{2}+b^{2}}{4}}}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>and hence independent of point <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle P}">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Point_construction">Point construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Point construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-pasc4-s.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Hyperbel-pasc4-s.svg/220px-Hyperbel-pasc4-s.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Hyperbel-pasc4-s.svg/330px-Hyperbel-pasc4-s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Hyperbel-pasc4-s.svg/440px-Hyperbel-pasc4-s.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="254" data-file-height="196" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-pasc4-s.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Point construction: asymptotes and <i>P</i><sub>1</sub> are given → <i>P</i><sub>2</sub></div></div></div>

<dd>are collinear with the center of the hyperbola (see diagram).</dd></dl>
<p>The simple proof is a consequence of the equation  <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\tfrac {1}{t_{1}}}{\vec {a}}={\tfrac {1}{t_{2}}}{\vec {b}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
            <mfrac>
              <mn>1</mn>
              <msub>
                <mi>t</mi>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>1</mn>
                </mrow>
              </msub>
            </mfrac>
          </mstyle>
        </mrow>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mover>
              <mi>a</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
            </mover>
          </mrow>
        </mrow>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
            <mfrac>
              <mn>1</mn>
              <msub>
                <mi>t</mi>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>2</mn>
                </mrow>
              </msub>
            </mfrac>
          </mstyle>
        </mrow>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mover>
              <mi>b</mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
            </mover>
          </mrow>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\tfrac {1}{t_{1}}}{\vec {a}}={\tfrac {1}{t_{2}}}{\vec {b}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/26075c30855a08485eb0284aeac4e114149ea02c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.505ex; width:9.945ex; height:4.009ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\tfrac {1}{t_{1}}}{\vec {a}}={\tfrac {1}{t_{2}}}{\vec {b}}}"/></span>.
</p><p>This property provides a possibility to construct points of a hyperbola if the asymptotes and one point are given.
</p><p>This property of a hyperbola is an affine version of the 4-point-degeneration of <a href="/wiki/Pascal%27s_theorem" title="Pascal&#39;s theorem">Pascal's theorem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tangent-asymptotes-triangle">Tangent-asymptotes-triangle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Tangent-asymptotes-triangle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-tad-s.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Hyperbel-tad-s.svg/220px-Hyperbel-tad-s.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Hyperbel-tad-s.svg/330px-Hyperbel-tad-s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Hyperbel-tad-s.svg/440px-Hyperbel-tad-s.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="289" data-file-height="234" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-tad-s.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbola: tangent-asymptotes-triangle</div></div></div>
<p>For simplicity the center of the hyperbola may be the origin and the  vectors <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\vec {f}}_{1},{\vec {f}}_{2}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e4791abac2946331d4756d50f7426d986a2d6000" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:13.192ex; height:3.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle |\det({\vec {f}}_{1},{\vec {f}}_{2})|}"/></span> is the area of the rhombus generated by <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\vec {f}}_{1},{\vec {f}}_{2}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mover>
                <mi>f</mi>
                <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
              </mover>
            </mrow>
          </mrow>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>1</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <msub>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mover>
                <mi>f</mi>
                <mo stretchy="false">&#x2192;<!-- → --></mo>
              </mover>
            </mrow>
          </mrow>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\vec {f}}_{1},{\vec {f}}_{2}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2d675df07212c5fa8c2ed45f7029276cf8ac79c7" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:6.472ex; height:3.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\vec {f}}_{1},{\vec {f}}_{2}}"/></span>. The area of a rhombus is equal to one half of the product of its diagonals. The diagonals are the semi-axes <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle a,b}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>a</mi>
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mi>b</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a,b}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/181523deba732fda302fd176275a0739121d3bc8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.261ex; height:2.509ex;" alt="a,b"/></span> of the hyperbola. Hence:
</p>
<dl><dd>The <i>area</i> of the triangle <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle MCD}">

        <mi>D</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>

  </semantics>

  <semantics>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Polar_coordinates">Polar coordinates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Polar coordinates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-pold-f-s.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Hyperbel-pold-f-s.svg/220px-Hyperbel-pold-f-s.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Hyperbel-pold-f-s.svg/330px-Hyperbel-pold-f-s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Hyperbel-pold-f-s.svg/440px-Hyperbel-pold-f-s.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="219" data-file-height="167" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-pold-f-s.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbola: Polar coordinates with pole = focus</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-pold-m-s.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Hyperbel-pold-m-s.svg/220px-Hyperbel-pold-m-s.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Hyperbel-pold-m-s.svg/330px-Hyperbel-pold-m-s.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Hyperbel-pold-m-s.svg/440px-Hyperbel-pold-m-s.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="219" data-file-height="164" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbel-pold-m-s.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbola: Polar coordinates with pole = center</div></div></div>
<p><b>For pole = focus: </b>
</p><p>The polar coordinates used most commonly for the hyperbola are defined relative to the Cartesian coordinate system that has its <i>origin in a focus</i> and its x-axis pointing towards the origin of the "canonical coordinate system" as illustrated in the first diagram.<br />
In this case the angle <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \varphi }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03C6;<!-- φ --></mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \varphi }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/33ee699558d09cf9d653f6351f9fda0b2f4aaa3e" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:1.52ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\varphi "/></span> is called <b>true anomaly</b>.
</p><p>Relative to this coordinate system one has that
</p>

<p>and
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle -\arccos \left(-{\frac {1}{e}}\right)&lt;\varphi &lt;\arccos \left(-{\frac {1}{e}}\right).}">

</p><p>With polar coordinates relative to the "canonical coordinate system" (see second diagram)
one has that

<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle r={\frac {b}{\sqrt {e^{2}\cos ^{2}\varphi -1}}}.\,}">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parametric_equations">Parametric equations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Parametric equations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A hyperbola with equation <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\tfrac {x^{2}}{a^{2}}}-{\tfrac {y^{2}}{b^{2}}}=1}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
            <mfrac>
              <msup>
                <mi>x</mi>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>2</mn>
                </mrow>
              </msup>
              <msup>
                <mi>a</mi>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>2</mn>
                </mrow>
              </msup>
            </mfrac>
          </mstyle>
        </mrow>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>2</mn>
                </mrow>
              </msup>

                <mi>b</mi>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>2</mn>
                </mrow>
              </msup>
            </mfrac>
          </mstyle>
        </mrow>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mn>1</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\tfrac {x^{2}}{a^{2}}}-{\tfrac {y^{2}}{b^{2}}}=1}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f18d979f7a463de6227020a06a2652f7f0c03f91" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.671ex; width:12.198ex; height:4.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\tfrac {x^{2}}{a^{2}}}-{\tfrac {y^{2}}{b^{2}}}=1}"/></span> can be described by several parametric equations:
</p>
<dl><dd><b>1:</b> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \left\{{\begin{matrix}\quad \;x\,=\,\pm a\cosh t\\y\,=\,b\sinh t\end{matrix}}\right.\quad ,\ t\in \mathbb {R} \ .}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow>
          <mo>{</mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mtable rowspacing="4pt" columnspacing="1em">
              <mtr>
                <mtd>
                  <mspace width="1em" />
                  <mspace width="thickmathspace" />
                  <mi>x</mi>
                  <mspace width="thinmathspace" />

                  <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
                  <mo>&#x00B1;<!-- ± --></mo>

                  <mi>cosh</mi>
                  <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
                  <mi>t</mi>
                </mtd>
              </mtr>
              <mtr>
                <mtd>
                  <mi>y</mi>
                  <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
                  <mo>=</mo>
                  <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
                  <mi>b</mi>
                  <mi>sinh</mi>
                  <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
                  <mi>t</mi>

            </mtable>
          </mrow>
          <mo fence="true" stretchy="true" symmetric="true"></mo>
        </mrow>
        <mspace width="1em" />
        <mo>,</mo>
        <mtext>&#xA0;</mtext>
        <mi>t</mi>
        <mo>&#x2208;<!-- ∈ --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mi mathvariant="double-struck">R</mi>
        </mrow>
        <mtext>&#xA0;</mtext>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \left\{{\begin{matrix}\quad \;x\,=\,\pm a\cosh t\\y\,=\,b\sinh t\end{matrix}}\right.\quad ,\ t\in \mathbb {R} \ .}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b47f0c08bcfd20a2a8553d8f7e86fed01fc4a9db" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:30.63ex; height:6.176ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \left\{{\begin{matrix}\quad \;x\,=\,\pm a\cosh t\\y\,=\,b\sinh t\end{matrix}}\right.\quad ,\ t\in \mathbb {R} \ .}"/></span></dd>
<dd><b>2:</b> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \left\{{\begin{matrix}\quad \ x\,=\,\pm a\,{\tfrac {t^{2}+1}{2t}}\\y\,=\,b\,{\tfrac {t^{2}-1}{2t}}\end{matrix}}\right.\quad ,\ t&gt;0\ .}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow>
          <mo>{</mo>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mtable rowspacing="4pt" columnspacing="1em">
              <mtr>
                <mtd>
                  <mspace width="1em" />
                  <mtext>&#xA0;</mtext>
                  <mi>x</mi>
                  <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
                  <mo>=</mo>
                  <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
                  <mo>&#x00B1;<!-- ± --></mo>
                  <mi>a</mi>
                  <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
                      <mfrac>
                        <mrow>
                          <msup>
                            <mi>t</mi>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_mathematical_definitions">Other mathematical definitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Other mathematical definitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reciprocation_of_a_circle">Reciprocation of a circle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Reciprocation of a circle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Reciprocation_(geometry)" class="mw-redirect" title="Reciprocation (geometry)">reciprocation</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Circle" title="Circle">circle</a> <i>B</i> in a circle <i>C</i> always yields a conic section such as a hyperbola. The process of "reciprocation in a circle <i>C</i>" consists of replacing every line and point in a geometrical figure with their corresponding <a href="/wiki/Pole_and_polar" title="Pole and polar">pole and polar</a>, respectively. The <i>pole</i> of a line is the <a href="/wiki/Inversive_geometry#Circle_inversion" title="Inversive geometry">inversion</a> of its closest point to the circle <i>C</i>, whereas the polar of a point is the converse, namely, a line whose closest point to <i>C</i> is the inversion of the point.
</p><p>The eccentricity of the conic section obtained by reciprocation is the ratio of the distances between the two circles' centers to the radius <i>r</i> of reciprocation circle <i>C</i>. If <b>B</b> and <b>C</b> represent the points at the centers of the corresponding circles, then
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle e={\frac {\overline {BC}}{r}}.}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>e</mi>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mover>
              <mrow>
                <mi>B</mi>
                <mi>C</mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo accent="false">&#x00AF;<!-- ¯ --></mo>
            </mover>
            <mi>r</mi>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle e={\frac {\overline {BC}}{r}}.}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/afa801993331918287927ad32bb1a0baeaef60ee" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:9.378ex; height:6.009ex;" alt="&#10;e = \frac{\overline{BC}}{r}.&#10;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Since the eccentricity of a hyperbola is always greater than one, the center <b>B</b> must lie outside of the reciprocating circle <i>C</i>.
</p><p>This definition implies that the hyperbola is both the <a href="/wiki/Locus_(mathematics)" title="Locus (mathematics)">locus</a> of the poles of the tangent lines to the circle <i>B</i>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Envelope_(mathematics)" title="Envelope (mathematics)">envelope</a> of the polar lines of the points on <i>B</i>. Conversely, the circle <i>B</i> is the envelope of polars of points on the hyperbola, and the locus of poles of tangent lines to the hyperbola. Two tangent lines to <i>B</i> have no (finite) poles because they pass through the center <b>C</b> of the reciprocation circle <i>C</i>; the polars of the corresponding tangent points on <i>B</i> are the asymptotes of the hyperbola. The two branches of the hyperbola correspond to the two parts of the circle <i>B</i> that are separated by these tangent points.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quadratic_equation">Quadratic equation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Quadratic equation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A hyperbola can also be defined as a second-degree equation in the Cartesian coordinates (<i>x</i>, <i>y</i>) in the <a href="/wiki/Plane_(geometry)" title="Plane (geometry)">plane</a>,
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle A_{xx}x^{2}+2A_{xy}xy+A_{yy}y^{2}+2B_{x}x+2B_{y}y+C=0,}">

<p>The principal axes of the hyperbola make an angle <i>&#966;</i> with the positive <i>x</i>-axis that is given by
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \tan 2\varphi ={\frac {2A_{xy}}{A_{xx}-A_{yy}}}.}">

        <mi>tan</mi>
        <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
        <mn>2</mn>
        <mi>&#x03C6;<!-- φ --></mi>
        <mo>=</mo>

  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/891a975463cdbfe2f531df05c03c9a6045d01207" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:21.316ex; height:6.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \tan 2\varphi ={\frac {2A_{xy}}{A_{xx}-A_{yy}}}.}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Rotating the coordinate axes so that the <i>x</i>-axis is aligned with the transverse axis brings the equation into its <b>canonical form</b>
</p>

<p>The normal line is perpendicular to the tangent line, and both pass through the same point (<i>x</i><sub>0</sub>, <i>y</i><sub>0</sub>).
</p><p>From the equation

<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {x^{2}}{a^{2}}}-{\frac {y^{2}}{b^{2}}}=1,\qquad 0&lt;b\leq a,}">

  </semantics>

<p>the left focus is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle (-ae,0)}">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Conic_section_analysis_of_the_hyperbolic_appearance_of_circles">Conic section analysis of the hyperbolic appearance of circles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Conic section analysis of the hyperbolic appearance of circles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zp-Kugel-Augp-innen.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Zp-Kugel-Augp-innen.svg/350px-Zp-Kugel-Augp-innen.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="277" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Zp-Kugel-Augp-innen.svg/525px-Zp-Kugel-Augp-innen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Zp-Kugel-Augp-innen.svg/700px-Zp-Kugel-Augp-innen.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="434" data-file-height="343" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zp-Kugel-Augp-innen.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Central_projection" class="mw-redirect" title="Central projection">Central projection</a> of circles on a sphere: The center <i>O</i> of projection is inside the sphere, the image plane is red. <br /> As images of the circles one gets a circle (magenta), ellipses, hyperbolas and lines. The special case of a parabola does not appear in this example.<br /> (If center <i>O</i> were <i>on</i> the sphere, all images of the circles would be circles or lines; see <a href="/wiki/Stereographic_projection" title="Stereographic projection">stereographic projection</a>).</div></div></div>
<p>Besides providing a uniform description of circles, ellipses, parabolas, and hyperbolas, conic sections can also be understood as a natural model of the geometry of perspective in the case where the scene being viewed consists of circles, or more generally an ellipse. The viewer is typically a camera or the human eye and the image of the scene a <a href="/wiki/Central_projection" class="mw-redirect" title="Central projection">central projection</a> onto an image plane, that is, all projection rays pass a fixed point <i>O</i>, the center. The <b>lens plane</b> is a plane parallel to the image plane at the lens <i>O</i>.
</p><p>The image of a circle c is 
</p>
<dl><dd>a) a <b>circle</b>, if circle <i>c</i> is in a special position, for example parallel to the image plane and others (see stereographic projection),</dd>
<dd>b) an <b>ellipse</b>, if <i>c</i> has <i>no</i> point with the lens plane in common,</dd>
<dd>c) a <b>parabola</b>, if <i>c</i> has <i>one</i> point with the lens plane in common and</dd>
<dd>d) a <b>hyperbola</b>, if <i>c</i> has <i>two</i> points with the lens plane in common.</dd></dl>
<p>(Special positions where the circle plane contains point <i>O</i> are omitted.)
</p><p>These results can be understood if one recognizes that the projection process can be seen in two steps: 1) circle c and point <i>O</i> generate a cone which is 2) cut by the image plane, in order to generate the image.
</p><p>One sees a hyperbola whenever catching sight of a portion of a circle cut by one's lens plane. The inability to see very much of the arms of the visible branch, combined with the complete absence of the second branch, makes it virtually impossible for the human visual system to recognize the connection with hyperbolas.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arc_length">Arc length</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Arc length">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
