<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Derived_curves">Derived curves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Derived curves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinusoidal_spirals.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Sinusoidal_spirals.svg/198px-Sinusoidal_spirals.svg.png" decoding="async" width="198" height="371" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Sinusoidal_spirals.svg/297px-Sinusoidal_spirals.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Sinusoidal_spirals.svg/396px-Sinusoidal_spirals.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sinusoidal_spirals.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sinusoidal_spiral" title="Sinusoidal spiral">Sinusoidal spirals</a>: equilateral <a class="mw-selflink selflink">hyperbola</a> (<span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> = −2</span>), line (<span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> = −1</span>), <a href="/wiki/Parabola" title="Parabola">parabola</a> (<span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> = −<span role="math" class="sfrac nowrap tion" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;"><span class="num" style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">1</span><span class="slash visualhide">/</span><span class="den" style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">2</span></span></span>), <a href="/wiki/Cardioid" title="Cardioid">cardioid</a> (<span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> = <span role="math" class="sfrac nowrap tion" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;"><span class="num" style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">1</span><span class="slash visualhide">/</span><span class="den" style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">2</span></span></span>), <a href="/wiki/Circle" title="Circle">circle</a> (<span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> = 1</span>) and <a href="/wiki/Lemniscate_of_Bernoulli" title="Lemniscate of Bernoulli">lemniscate of Bernoulli</a> (<span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> = 2</span>), where <span class="texhtml"><i>r<sup>n</sup></i> = −1<sup><i>n</i></sup> cos <i>nθ</i></span> in <a href="/wiki/Polar_coordinates" class="mw-redirect" title="Polar coordinates">polar coordinates</a> and their equivalents in <a href="/wiki/Rectangular_coordinates" class="mw-redirect" title="Rectangular coordinates">rectangular coordinates</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Several other curves can be derived from the hyperbola by <a href="/wiki/Inversive_geometry#Circle_inversion" title="Inversive geometry">inversion</a>, the so-called <a href="/wiki/Inverse_curve" title="Inverse curve">inverse curves</a> of the hyperbola. If the center of inversion is chosen as the hyperbola's own center, the inverse curve is the <a href="/wiki/Lemniscate_of_Bernoulli" title="Lemniscate of Bernoulli">lemniscate of Bernoulli</a>; the lemniscate is also the envelope of circles centered on a rectangular hyperbola and passing through the origin. If the center of inversion is chosen at a focus or a vertex of the hyperbola, the resulting inverse curves are a <a href="/wiki/Lima%C3%A7on" title="Limaçon">limaçon</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Strophoid" title="Strophoid">strophoid</a>, respectively.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Elliptic_coordinates">Elliptic coordinates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Elliptic coordinates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A family of confocal hyperbolas is the basis of the system of <a href="/wiki/Elliptic_coordinates" class="mw-redirect" title="Elliptic coordinates">elliptic coordinates</a> in two dimensions. These hyperbolas are described by the equation
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \left({\frac {x}{c\cos \theta }}\right)^{2}-\left({\frac {y}{c\sin \theta }}\right)^{2}=1}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msup>
          <mrow>
            <mo>(</mo>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mfrac>
                <mi>x</mi>
                <mrow>
                  <mi>c</mi>
                  <mi>cos</mi>
                  <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
                  <mi>&#x03B8;<!-- θ --></mi>
                </mrow>
              </mfrac>
            </mrow>
            <mo>)</mo>
          </mrow>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <msup>
          <mrow>
            <mo>(</mo>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mfrac>
                <mi>y</mi>
                <mrow>
                  <mi>c</mi>
                  <mi>sin</mi>
                  <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
                  <mi>&#x03B8;<!-- θ --></mi>
                </mrow>
              </mfrac>
            </mrow>
            <mo>)</mo>
          </mrow>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msup>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mn>1</mn>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \left({\frac {x}{c\cos \theta }}\right)^{2}-\left({\frac {y}{c\sin \theta }}\right)^{2}=1}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e30facddd46ccd09416f05ce6704e19f20e2160b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:28.143ex; height:5.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \left({\frac {x}{c\cos \theta }}\right)^{2}-\left({\frac {y}{c\sin \theta }}\right)^{2}=1}"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where the foci are located at a distance <i>c</i> from the origin on the <i>x</i>-axis, and where θ is the angle of the asymptotes with the <i>x</i>-axis. Every hyperbola in this family is orthogonal to every ellipse that shares the same foci. This orthogonality may be shown by a <a href="/wiki/Conformal_map" title="Conformal map">conformal map</a> of the Cartesian coordinate system <i>w</i> = <i>z</i> + 1/<i>z</i>, where <i>z</i>= <i>x</i> + <i>iy</i> are the original Cartesian coordinates, and <i>w</i>=<i>u</i> + <i>iv</i> are those after the transformation.
</p><p>Other orthogonal two-dimensional coordinate systems involving hyperbolas may be obtained by other conformal mappings. For example, the mapping <i>w</i> = <i>z</i><sup>2</sup> transforms the Cartesian coordinate system into two families of orthogonal hyperbolas.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_properties_of_hyperbolas">Other properties of hyperbolas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Other properties of hyperbolas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>The following are <a href="/wiki/Concurrent_lines" title="Concurrent lines">concurrent</a>: (1) a circle passing through the hyperbola's foci and centered at the hyperbola's center; (2) either of the lines that are tangent to the hyperbola at the vertices; and (3) either of the asymptotes of the hyperbola.<sup id="cite_ref-web4_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web4-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-web1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The following are also concurrent: (1) the circle that is centered at the hyperbola's center and that passes through the hyperbola's vertices; (2) either directrix; and (3) either of the asymptotes.<sup id="cite_ref-web1_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Akademia_Ekonomiczna_w_Krakowie_Pawilon_C.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Akademia_Ekonomiczna_w_Krakowie_Pawilon_C.JPG/220px-Akademia_Ekonomiczna_w_Krakowie_Pawilon_C.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Akademia_Ekonomiczna_w_Krakowie_Pawilon_C.JPG/330px-Akademia_Ekonomiczna_w_Krakowie_Pawilon_C.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Akademia_Ekonomiczna_w_Krakowie_Pawilon_C.JPG/440px-Akademia_Ekonomiczna_w_Krakowie_Pawilon_C.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Akademia_Ekonomiczna_w_Krakowie_Pawilon_C.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hyperbolas as declination lines on a sundial</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sundials">Sundials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sundials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hyperbolas may be seen in many <a href="/wiki/Sundial" title="Sundial">sundials</a>. On any given day, the sun revolves in a circle on the <a href="/wiki/Celestial_sphere" title="Celestial sphere">celestial sphere</a>, and its rays striking the point on a sundial traces out a cone of light. The intersection of this cone with the horizontal plane of the ground forms a conic section. At most populated latitudes and at most times of the year, this conic section is a hyperbola. In practical terms, the shadow of the tip of a pole traces out a hyperbola on the ground over the course of a day (this path is called the <i>declination line</i>). The shape of this hyperbola varies with the geographical latitude and with the time of the year, since those factors affect the cone of the sun's rays relative to the horizon. The collection of such hyperbolas for a whole year at a given location was called a <i>pelekinon</i> by the Greeks, since it resembles a double-bladed axe.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Multilateration">Multilateration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Multilateration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A hyperbola is the basis for solving <a href="/wiki/Multilateration" title="Multilateration">multilateration</a> problems, the task of locating a point from the differences in its distances to given points — or, equivalently, the difference in arrival times of synchronized signals between the point and the given points. Such problems are important in navigation, particularly on water; a ship can locate its position from the difference in arrival times of signals from a <a href="/wiki/LORAN" title="LORAN">LORAN</a> or <a href="/wiki/GPS" class="mw-redirect" title="GPS">GPS</a> transmitters. Conversely, a homing beacon or any transmitter can be located by comparing the arrival times of its signals at two separate receiving stations; such techniques may be used to track objects and people. In particular, the set of possible positions of a point that has a distance difference of 2<i>a</i> from two given points is a hyperbola of vertex separation 2<i>a</i> whose foci are the two given points.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Path_followed_by_a_particle">Path followed by a particle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Path followed by a particle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The path followed by any particle in the classical <a href="/wiki/Kepler_problem" title="Kepler problem">Kepler problem</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Conic_section" title="Conic section">conic section</a>. In particular, if the total energy <i>E</i> of the particle is greater than zero (that is, if the particle is unbound), the path of such a particle is a hyperbola. This property is useful in studying atomic and sub-atomic forces by scattering high-energy particles; for example, the <a href="/wiki/Geiger%E2%80%93Marsden_experiment" title="Geiger–Marsden experiment">Rutherford experiment</a> demonstrated the existence of an <a href="/wiki/Atomic_nucleus" title="Atomic nucleus">atomic nucleus</a> by examining the scattering of <a href="/wiki/Alpha_particle" title="Alpha particle">alpha particles</a> from <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> atoms. If the short-range nuclear interactions are ignored, the atomic nucleus and the alpha particle interact only by a repulsive <a href="/wiki/Coulomb%27s_law" title="Coulomb&#39;s law">Coulomb force</a>, which satisfies the <a href="/wiki/Inverse_square_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Inverse square law">inverse square law</a> requirement for a Kepler problem.
</p>
<h3><span id="Korteweg.E2.80.93de_Vries_equation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Korteweg–de_Vries_equation">Korteweg–de Vries equation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Korteweg–de Vries equation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The hyperbolic trig function <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \operatorname {sech} \,x}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>sech</mi>
        <mspace width="thinmathspace" />
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \operatorname {sech} \,x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3cc03899287be4abc7eee4c8171592f26dc4c49d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.377ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\operatorname{sech}\, x"/></span> appears as one solution to the <a href="/wiki/Korteweg%E2%80%93de_Vries_equation" title="Korteweg–de Vries equation">Korteweg–de Vries equation</a> which describes the motion of a soliton wave in a canal.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angle_trisection">Angle trisection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Angle trisection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbola_angle_trisection.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hyperbola_angle_trisection.svg/220px-Hyperbola_angle_trisection.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hyperbola_angle_trisection.svg/330px-Hyperbola_angle_trisection.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Hyperbola_angle_trisection.svg/440px-Hyperbola_angle_trisection.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyperbola_angle_trisection.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trisecting an angle (AOB) using a hyperbola of eccentricity 2 (yellow curve)</div></div></div>
<p>As shown first by <a href="/wiki/Apollonius_of_Perga" title="Apollonius of Perga">Apollonius of Perga</a>, a hyperbola can be used to <a href="/wiki/Angle_trisection" title="Angle trisection">trisect any angle</a>, a well studied problem of geometry. Given an angle, first draw a circle centered at its vertex <b>O</b>, which intersects the sides of the angle at points <b>A</b> and <b>B</b>. Next draw the line segment with endpoints  <b>A</b> and <b>B</b> and its perpendicular bisector <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \ell }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x2113;<!-- ℓ --></mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \ell }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f066e981e530bacc07efc6a10fa82deee985929e" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.97ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\ell "/></span>. Construct a hyperbola of <a href="/wiki/Eccentricity_(mathematics)" title="Eccentricity (mathematics)">eccentricity</a> <i>e</i>=2 with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \ell }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x2113;<!-- ℓ --></mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \ell }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f066e981e530bacc07efc6a10fa82deee985929e" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.97ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\ell "/></span> as <a href="/wiki/Directrix_(conic_section)" class="mw-redirect" title="Directrix (conic section)">directrix</a> and <b>B</b> as a focus. Let <b>P</b> be the intersection (upper) of the hyperbola with the circle. Angle <b>POB</b> trisects angle <b>AOB</b>.
</p><p>To prove this, reflect the line segment <b>OP</b> about the line <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \ell }">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x2113;<!-- ℓ --></mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \ell }</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f066e981e530bacc07efc6a10fa82deee985929e" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.97ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="\ell "/></span> obtaining the point <b>P'</b> as the image of <b>P</b>. Segment <b>AP'</b> has the same length as segment <b>BP</b> due to the reflection, while segment <b>PP'</b> has the same length as segment <b>BP</b> due to the eccentricity of the hyperbola. As <b>OA</b>, <b>OP'</b>, <b>OP</b> and <b>OB</b> are all radii of the same circle (and so, have the same length), the triangles <b>OAP'</b>, <b>OPP'</b> and <b>OPB</b> are all congruent. Therefore, the angle has been trisected, since 3×<b>POB</b> = <b>AOB</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Efficient_portfolio_frontier">Efficient portfolio frontier</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Efficient portfolio frontier">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Modern_portfolio_theory#The_efficient_frontier_with_no_risk-free_asset" title="Modern portfolio theory">portfolio theory</a>, the locus of <a href="/wiki/Mean_variance_efficiency" class="mw-redirect" title="Mean variance efficiency">mean-variance efficient</a> portfolios (called the efficient frontier) is the upper half of the east-opening branch of a hyperbola drawn with the portfolio return's standard deviation plotted horizontally and its expected value plotted vertically; according to this theory, all rational investors would choose a portfolio characterized by some point on this locus.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biochemistry">Biochemistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Biochemistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">biochemistry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pharmacology" title="Pharmacology">pharmacology</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hill_equation_(biochemistry)" title="Hill equation (biochemistry)">Hill equation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hill_equation_(biochemistry)" title="Hill equation (biochemistry)">Hill-Langmuir equation</a> respectively describe biological <a href="/wiki/Stimulus%E2%80%93response_model" title="Stimulus–response model">responses</a> and the formation of <a href="/wiki/Protein%E2%80%93ligand_complex" title="Protein–ligand complex">protein–ligand complexes</a> as functions of ligand concentration. They are both rectangular hyperbolae.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hyperbolas_as_plane_sections_of_quadrics">Hyperbolas as plane sections of quadrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Hyperbolas as plane sections of quadrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hyperbolas appear as plane sections of the following <a href="/wiki/Quadric" title="Quadric">quadrics</a>:
</p>
<ul><li>Elliptic <a href="/wiki/Cone" title="Cone">cone</a></li>
<li>Hyperbolic <a href="/wiki/Cylinder" title="Cylinder">cylinder</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hyperbolic_paraboloid" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperbolic paraboloid">Hyperbolic paraboloid</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hyperboloid_of_one_sheet" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperboloid of one sheet">Hyperboloid of one sheet</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hyperboloid_of_two_sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperboloid of two sheets">Hyperboloid of two sheets</a></li></ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_related_topics">Other related topics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hyperbola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Other related topics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
